Cruel Case of Daughter-in-Law Biting Mother-in-Law

Yeh Chang's jealousy over her sister-in-law's three thousand yuan dowry

Old woman has six bite wounds on her lower legs

Old Mrs. Yeh Huang, a local resident, lives in a bungalow at the end of Kang Ji Lane, Kang Ti Road, in the French Concession. She is sixty years old and has two sons and one daughter. The family has ancestral properties worth around thirty to forty thousand yuan. The eldest son, A-Fu, is thirty-two years old and married to Chang (thirty-seven years old this year). The second son, Mao-Qing, is twenty-nine years old and married to Lu (twenty-nine years old this year). Both have children. The youngest daughter, Cui-Bao (nickname A-Liu), is twenty-seven years old this year and not yet engaged, awaiting marriage. However, the eldest daughter-in-law, Chang, is known to be fierce, nicknamed "She-Tiger." Matchmakers and neighbors are aware of her reputation, so the relationship between mother-in-law, daughter-in-law, and sisters-in-law is not harmonious. Mrs. Huang, being elderly, cannot withstand Chang's fierce abuse, so she lives with her second son in the old house. Chang and her husband, A-Fu, live separately nearby at No. 4, Lane 454, Kang Ti Road. The brothers each make a living and do not visit often. Cui-Bao works at the Mayer Silk Weaving Factory. Over the years, she met Chen Qiao, an accountant at the factory, and their friendship developed into love. They have been secretly dating for two years. Recently, the two parties decided to officially marry, with matchmakers and witnesses arranging the marriage. Cui-Bao also asked her mother for autonomy in marriage. With Mrs. Huang's permission, the wedding was set for the 10th of this month (i.e., the 6th day of the third month of the lunar calendar). Mrs. Huang was preparing the dowry, bridal clothes, and utensils, which were estimated to cost around one thousand yuan. Unexpectedly, Chang became jealous when she saw her mother-in-law preparing a large sum to marry off her daughter. On the 7th of this month, she went to the old house to extort a large sum from her mother-in-law, demanding three thousand yuan, saying, "You have money to marry off your daughter, so I also want three thousand yuan from you." Her demands were unreasonable, and Mrs. Huang sternly refused. The mother-in-law and daughter-in-law started arguing, and people intervened to break it up. Chang went home resentfully, holding a grudge. That night, around 10 p.m., she sneaked back to the old house. Taking advantage of her mother-in-law and Cui-Bao sleeping soundly, she pried open the door and entered. She got on the bed and straddled Mrs. Huang without asking any questions. She used her mouth to bite her mother-in-law's lower body, both legs, and genitals. Mrs. Huang woke up in pain from her sleep. Being old and unable to resist, she was bitten six times, with skin and flesh torn off. Cui-Bao, fearing Chang's fierceness, got out of bed and hid. Mrs. Huang shouted for help, and her second daughter-in-law, Lu, and neighbors responded. Chang took the opportunity to escape. Later, Lu and Cui-Bao entered the room to check on Mrs. Huang. She was in extreme pain and had fainted. Inspecting the injuries on her lower body, they saw a bloody mess, too gruesome to bear. They immediately found a way to take her to Guangci Hospital for treatment. Unexpectedly, Chang was still not satisfied. The next morning (the 8th), she learned that her brother-in-law, Mao-Qing, and his wife, and her sister-in-law, Cui-Bao, were accompanying Mrs. Huang at the hospital. She sneaked into the old house again and burned all forty-eight pieces of Cui-Bao's prepared dowry, including silk and cotton, lined and unlined bridal clothes (worth 486 yuan), in the courtyard. She also took all the gold, silver, and jewelry worth 351 yuan and fled to hide with Ah Gui-jie Yi Zhong. When Cui-Bao returned home and saw the scene, she was terrified by her sister-in-law's cruelty and her obstruction of the wedding. She was also heartbroken that her mother was injured because of her. She told her fiancé, and they went to the Lujiawan Central Police Station to request an investigation. The police chief, seeing Chang's barbarity, deemed it a serious violation of human ethics and sent detectives to arrest her. However, Chang was nowhere to be found and could not be arrested. They photographed the remaining ashes of the clothes and brought them back to the police station in a bamboo basket to report to the police chief. Chang, hiding outside, saw the severity of the situation. On the afternoon of the 14th, she sneaked back home and pretended to commit suicide by swallowing a gold ring. Detective Zhu Caichen learned of this and rushed to arrest her, taking her into custody at the police station. Yesterday afternoon, she was sent to the Second Special District Local Court for investigation. Judge Wang Gangxu, along with clerk Zhu Chengzhu, and prosecutor Wu Xiaoshu, presided over the interrogation in the First Criminal Court. First, police lawyer Fei Xizhen presented the case, accusing her of violating Articles 294, 298, and 382 of the Criminal Code, including harming a senior relative and destroying property. He stated that the police procedures were not yet complete and requested a postponement for further investigation. He also presented the ashes of the clothes as evidence. The victim, Mrs. Yeh Huang, was escorted to the court by her second daughter-in-law, Lu, and daughter, Cui-Bao. Due to the severity of her injuries, she could not stand, so the court allowed her to sit during the hearing. Lawyer Yeh Fu-kang represented her and described the defendant's biting. When questioned, the defendant, Yeh Chang, denied biting her mother-in-law's body, claiming that her sister-in-law, Lu, and sister-in-law, Cui, had bitten her and falsely accused her. She hired a lawyer to defend her and requested bail during the postponement. The court, considering the seriousness of the case, denied the defendant's request for bail and adjourned the hearing. The defendant was temporarily detained at the police station, and the victim was ordered to have her injuries examined by the coroner at 2:30 p.m. that afternoon for verification. During the hearing, neighbors, relatives, and Cui-Bao's fiancé, Chen Qiao, and friends were present, crowding the courtroom. Only after the hearing was adjourned did the crowd disperse.

Case of Prostitute Dying from Abortion

Zheng Qingtang and others sentenced separately

Zheng Qingtang, from Hangzhou, and his wife, Zheng Shen, ran a brothel at No. 27 Guangxi Road. In December of last year, they bought a girl from Hangzhou named Shen Xianghong for 400 yuan with the intention of making her a prostitute. However, Shen was pregnant and could not receive guests. They asked Wu Xiubao, a woman from Hangzhou (nicknamed Lao Er), to introduce Wang Laoniang to perform an abortion on Shen. Due to the poor medical skills, Shen died from the abortion. Afterward, they prepared a coffin for Shen and claimed she died of illness, placing her coffin in the Shaoxing Guild Hall in the South City. Later, the Zhabei Police Station discovered this and arrested Zheng and his wife, as well as Wu Xiubao, and brought them to the First Special District Court for interrogation. The court sent a letter to the local court to conduct an autopsy. The autopsy confirmed that Shen died from the abortion. After the interrogation, the sentencing was scheduled for yesterday morning. Police lawyer Ru Bao-yi and the defendant's lawyer, Yuan Yang-an, were present in court. Judge Qian Hongye announced the verdict: Zheng Qingtang, intending to profit, enticed a girl under the age of twenty and was sentenced to one year of imprisonment. The charge of performing an abortion was dismissed. Zheng Shen, intending to profit, enticed a girl under the age of twenty and was sentenced to one year of imprisonment. Intending to profit from an abortion, which resulted in the death of a woman, she was sentenced to four years of imprisonment and fined 300 yuan. The sentence was four years and six months, and the fine was 300 yuan. If the fine was not paid, it would be converted to one day of imprisonment for every two yuan. Wu Xiubao, intending to profit from an abortion, which resulted in the death of a woman, was sentenced to one year and six months of imprisonment. The number of days each of the three individuals was detained before the final verdict was reached would be counted as two days of imprisonment for each day of detention.

Autopsy of Sun Jinxiang's Body

Car driver confirmed to be at fault

Police have filed charges

The previous day, at around 1 p.m., Zhou Changjin, a driver from Funing, driving truck No. 16876, was traveling south on Bai Li Nan Road and turned west onto Yi Ding Pan Road, hitting and killing pedestrian Sun Jinxiang from Pudong, and injuring Pang Zhou and Jin Yaoting. The details were reported in yesterday's newspaper. Sun Jinxiang's body was sent to the Fei Lun Road morgue by Police Officer No. 340 from the Jing'an Temple Police Station. Pang Zhou was sent to Guangren Hospital for treatment. The truck driver, Zhou Changjin, was taken to the police station. Yesterday morning, Prosecutor Li Ying from the First Special District Court, along with coroner Wei Ligong and clerk Wu Zuyi, went to the morgue to examine Sun's body. Later, they held a formal hearing. Zhou Changjin testified that he was 31 years old, lived at No. 4040 Maigen Road, and had been driving trucks for over two years. The other day, he was driving truck No. 16876 on Bai Li Nan Road and turned onto Yi Ding Pan Road. There were two people walking in the middle of the road on the south side of the road. He honked the horn, but they ignored him. As his truck turned, he had no choice but to steer north, which resulted in the accident. Liu Rongda testified that he and Jin Yaoting were sewing clothes in the No. 28 clothing store when the truck suddenly crashed into the store, destroying all the equipment. He was lucky to escape, but Yaoting was injured in the head and hands when the wall collapsed. Sun Jin's wife, Pang Manhe, also testified. Prosecutor Li concluded that the deceased, Sun Jinxiang, was confirmed to have been killed by truck No. 16876. The body was handed over to Sun's mother, Sun Jin, for burial. The truck driver, Zhou Changjin, was found to be at fault, and charges were filed. He was handed over to the police station for further investigation.

Liang Chengyu's Case Sent Back for Retrial

Liang Chengyu, a Chinese detective from the No. 2 Inspectorate of the General Police Department, was arrested and sent to the First Special District Court for allegedly robbing Fang Liansheng of morphine worth 50,000 yuan. The initial trial found Liang not guilty. The police department appealed to the High Court, and Liang was sentenced to ten years of imprisonment. However, Liang also appealed to the Supreme Court. Meanwhile, the police department filed another lawsuit with the Special Court, alleging that Liang had kidnapped Chen Shifan, the owner of the Chen Lin Ji Construction Factory, on Pingwang Street on December 19 of the previous year, and Li Huiqing, a property owner, on Hubei Road on February 8 of the previous year. After investigation, Liang was sentenced to death, and the report was submitted to the Jiangsu Provincial Government for approval. The Provincial Government considered there were still doubts about Liang's involvement in the kidnapping case, so it sent the case back to the Special Court for retrial. Yesterday afternoon, at 2 p.m., the further hearing was scheduled. The police department brought the accomplices and witnesses, including Fang Liansheng, and escorted Liang to the Second Criminal Court. Judge Wu Tingqi conducted the interrogation. The defendant Liang Chengyu's wife also attended the hearing and hired three lawyers, Zhan Jifeng, Yeh Fukan, and Yuan Yang-an, to defend him. Police lawyer Wang Yaotang stated that the court had ordered the police to summon the two kidnapped victims and the tea server from the Yadong Hotel. The police had sent detectives to summon them, but Li Huiqing was not in Shanghai, and Chen Shifan had been summoned but did not appear. The tea server from the Yadong Hotel could not be summoned because the hotel had changed owners and the tea server was no longer employed. Judge Wu stated that the case file was currently at the Supreme Court and had not yet been returned, so the trial could not proceed today. He ordered Liang to be returned to custody for a rescheduled hearing.

Xue and Qian, Two Traitors, Arrested

Transferred to Local Court Yesterday

The Municipal Security Bureau reported from the First Division of the Second District that Geng Changming, a detective from the 囗囗 Division, had arrested suspected traitors Bo Ming, a resident of Wuxi, 26 years old, living at No. 26 Zhongpi Lane in the city, a businessman, and Qian Xiangsheng, a resident of Chongming, 24 years old, who lived with Xue. A iron seal of the "North Shanghai People's Local Maintenance Association" and a ledger of the Fuhua Company were found on the two men. They were immediately sent to the Third Section for interrogation. The two confessed to having dealings with the puppet maintenance association in Zhabei. Director Wen, considering the case involved suspected traitors, ordered the section to transfer Xue and Qian, along with the evidence, to the Local Court for trial yesterday (the 15th).

Robbers Steal Wages from Wing On Textile Factory

3,950 Yuan in cash stolen

Last night at around 8 p.m., during wage distribution at the Wing On Textile Factory on Maigen Road, three robbers disguised as workers suddenly broke into the accounting room. One of them held a pistol and threatened them to remain silent. They stole 3,950 yuan in cash and escaped through the back door. The robbers fled in a truck waiting outside the door. At the time they fired a warning shot, but fortunately no one was injured. Afterward, the factory reported the incident to the police to investigate.

Case of Customs Launch Colliding and Drowning Female Workers

Over Twenty People Receive 100 Yuan Each

In the case of the Nanyang Tobacco Company ferry colliding with a customs launch, causing the drowning of over thirty female workers, Wang Xiaomei and others, the captain of the customs launch, have been detained by the Local Court. However, the customs authorities, considering that the victims' families were all poor, have agreed to provide 100 yuan in compensation to each family. An agreement has been reached with the Local Court that the court will issue certificates to the families of the deceased who can prove that their loved ones died in the accident, which they can use to claim compensation from customs. However, the victims' families argue that the cost of funeral arrangements exceeds 100 yuan and are demanding additional compensation, so the matter has not yet been fully resolved.

French Police Raid Opium Dens and Drug Pills

Ruifuli: The other day, the Political Affairs Office of the French General Police Department, acting on information from informants that reactionary elements were hiding at No. 17 Ruifuli, West Zilai Huo Street, attempting to hold secret meetings, sent Chinese and foreign detectives to the address to investigate. The investigation revealed no evidence of reactionary elements holding meetings. However, they discovered that the house was secretly manufacturing and selling red pills. They seized a large quantity of red pills and raw materials for white powder, and arrested the owner, a small Shandong man, and two accomplices, taking them to the police station to be sent to the court for investigation.

Baoxingli: Also, at around 10 p.m. on the same day, the Political Affairs Office cracked down on an opium den at No. 7 Baoxingli, East Xinqiao Street. They arrested twenty-four opium smokers and two operators, along with dozens of opium pipes and opium paste, and took them to the police station to be sent to the Local Court for investigation.

Shengpingli: Yesterday afternoon at around 7 p.m., Shen Defu, the Chief Chinese Inspector of the French Police Department, received a tip that there was a large-scale opium den at No. 19 Shengpingli, French Avenue, and requested a swift investigation. Chief Inspector Shen immediately led a team of detectives to the address and arrested three people and seized several opium paraphernalia. They were immediately taken to the police station and transferred to the court for interrogation.

Trial Opens in Pudong Inheritance Murder Case

Zhang Guoxiang and Zhang Yuxiang, of Huayuan Stone Bridge, Pudong, were shot and killed by Zhang Qingxiang, the son of their stepmother Zhang Zhang, and their maternal uncle, Zhang Quansheng, over an inheritance dispute. Guoxiang was injured but not killed, while Yuxiang died. The Local Court arrested Zhang Zhang, Zhang Qingxiang, and Zhang Quansheng and filed a public prosecution after a thorough investigation. Yesterday, Judge Shen opened the continued trial. Zhang Qiao stated that she was Zhang Linsen's second concubine, and Zhang Zhang was the first concubine. The first wife, Zhang Qian, and her husband were both dead. She did not know how this tragedy occurred. However, Zhang Quansheng was a frequent visitor. Zhang Qingxiang had been doing business on Quansheng's small steamboat the year before. When asked if Zhang Yuxiang had contact with Zhang Quansheng, she replied that they were not on good terms and did not associate because she had helped Zhang Qian's wife with a lawsuit after her husband's death. Zhang Yunxiang stated that he was Zhang Linsen's youngest son and was studying business at a customs brokerage. He had been at home since the boycott of Japanese goods. On the night of the incident, he was called away by a friend to play football and was away from home all day. Later, he saw the police running around while reading a newspaper in a rice store and learned about the incident. He went to see Guoxiang first, but did not find his sister-in-law. He then went home and told his mother, who already knew. Soon after, Qingxiang returned, and the family was speechless. Zhao Chunfu stated that he was a partner in a shoe store in Huayuan Stone Bridge. He had only recently joined the partnership. He was called to testify today, but his boss asked him to come in his place. He knew nothing about the matter. Zhang Shangzhen stated that he was an employee of the Pudong Bank. It was true that Zhang Guoxiang and Zhang Qingxiang had argued when they mortgaged forms at the bank. Zhang Baoshi, the wife of Zhang Guoxiang and Zhang Yuxiang, hired a lawyer to appear in court and requested an additional private prosecution for over 5,000 yuan. The judge stated that the witnesses were not all present and adjourned the hearing. The defendants were returned to custody.

Weather Report

The Zikawei Observatory's weather forecast for 4:30 p.m. yesterday stated that the Shandong coast was clear, the lower Yangtze River region was gradually becoming cloudy with occasional frost in some areas, and the area south of Ma'anshan Island was cloudy. There was a gentle northeast wind in the Taiwan Strait. The rest of the coastal areas and the Yangtze River region had gentle breezes of uncertain direction. The weather was bad in southeastern Japan. Also, in the twenty-four hours before 3 p.m. yesterday, the highest temperature in Shanghai was 70.7 degrees and the lowest was 49.8 degrees. On the same day last year, the highest temperature was 72.9 degrees and the lowest was 50.5 degrees.

The special train is now waiting at the station, but it will not depart before Sunday or Monday. At 12 p.m., they met with Qiu Changwei and other representatives of university professors. At 1 p.m., they met with Luo Longji and other representatives of reporters from Beiping and Tianjin. During the meeting with the professors from Peking University, they mentioned that Japan had a plan to send another 75,000 troops to the Northeast. They asked if the League of Nations could stop it. Lytton replied that the League of Nations could not recognize the results of any armed aggression and asked them not to worry too much. He also said that the Northeast problem arose between a strong and a weak country. If it could not be handled fairly, it would not only sow the seeds of disaster in the East but also hinder world peace. Lytton replied that the Inquiry Commission was well aware of the importance of this and would work hard to resolve it. (Dispatch of the 15th)

He asked the commission to pay attention to this during its investigation in the Northeast. Lytton and others were moved and expressed their gratitude for the opinions of the media. Japan Frequently Spreads News of Rejecting Gu

(Beiping) A diplomat said that the news of rejecting Gu was frequently spread, which clearly showed that Japan had a predetermined plan and intended to intimidate. He pointed out that when the Japanese representative Yoshida came to China with the Inquiry Commission, the Chinese side had prepared hotels, transportation, and public banquets in Beijing, Shanghai, Wuhan, and other places. Even his entourage was specially assigned commissioners to receive them and provide them with all kinds of conveniences, treating them with the courtesy of distinguished guests, considering them as one with the Inquiry Commission. Today, Japan was doing the opposite and obstructing representative Gu from performing his duties. Not only did the Inquiry Commission consider it contrary to international etiquette, but also feared that future Sino-Japanese relations would be even more untrustworthy. He hoped that insightful people in Japan would reflect on this. (Dispatch of the 15th)

League of Nations Investigation Team Receives Telegram from Ma Zhanshan

Circumstances of Feigned Compliance with the Japanese

The Japanese Manipulation of the Puppet State

(Beiping) Yesterday, the investigation team received a telegram from Ma Zhanshan,

The text was four to five thousand words long, recounting in detail his retreat to Hailun and subsequent feigned compliance with the Japanese. It also described the various oppressions and manipulations by the Japanese in creating the puppet state. The telegram included a daily diary starting from the day he retreated to Hailun until the present. It began by stating that when he retreated to Hailun, the Japanese military sent officials to implore Ma to return to the province, saying that if he agreed, the Japanese military would definitely not enter Heihe and that all matters would be under Ma's command. Ma resolutely returned to the province, only to find that after arriving, the situation changed drastically. The Japanese constantly monitored and oppressed him in various ways, and he realized he had fallen into their trap. Therefore, he had no choice but to feign cooperation in order to obtain various information. Now, he is reporting all Japanese conspiracies in detail to the investigation team for reference. One section describes how the Japanese military manipulated the puppet state, sending people to instruct Puyi that he must refuse the title of "Chief Executive" of the so-called "Manchukuo" before accepting it, otherwise he would face adverse consequences. He was closely monitored, and his words and actions were not given the slightest freedom. Puyi attempted suicide by poison three times, but each time he was discovered and rescued by the Japanese. It is reported that after the members of the investigation team, including Lord Lytton, understood the general meaning, they instructed the secretary to translate it into English for use as an important reference in the investigation. (15th Dispatch)

More Explosives Discovered Near Chenggaozi Station on the Eastern Railway

Statement Issued by Russian Director

(Harbin) On the morning of the 13th, more explosives were discovered near Cheng Gaozi Station on the Harbin-Suifenhe Line, buried under the railway tracks. They were discovered by Chadov. (15th Dispatch)

(Harbin) Regarding the derailment of the Japanese troop train near Cheng Gaozi Station, it has been investigated that the train consisted of 41 cars, 16 of which derailed and fell off a 20-foot high embankment. The first five cars caught fire due to a gasoline explosion, and the ammunition car also caught fire. The Japanese army officers, Captain Asazuma, Lieutenant Inoue, and 12 soldiers on board were burned to death. Twenty-seven junior officers and soldiers were injured, and more than 100 others suffered minor injuries. After the incident, the Japanese sent a troop train from Harbin to assist and rescued the dead and wounded from the wreckage. The fire was extinguished by 7:30 a.m. on the 13th. A Japanese aircraft arrived at the scene on the afternoon of the 13th to investigate and captured a passing Chinese, tied him to a utility pole, and ordered him to identify accomplices. Traffic was restored at 4:00 p.m. (15th Dispatch)

(Harbin) Regarding the derailment of the Japanese troop train on the Harbin-Suifenhe Line, the Japanese side has determined that it was the work of the Red Russians and has declared that the Eastern Railway must bear responsibility. Honjo has sent personnel to investigate, but has not yet submitted any demands. The Eastern Railway has formed an investigation committee to investigate the truth of the matter. (15th Dispatch)

(Harbin) On the 14th, Rudyi, the Russian director of the Eastern Railway, issued a statement regarding the derailment of the Japanese troop train, saying that on the 12th, explosives had been discovered 945 kilometers from Harbin, and after removing them, it was deemed safe. Unexpectedly, this tragedy occurred. The cause of the derailment was the removal of the spikes. He did not mention who was responsible for the sabotage. (15th Dispatch)

Japanese 10th Division to Station Permanently in Harbin

(Harbin) The Japanese 2nd Division has been ordered to return to Japan. The 10th Division will come to Harbin for permanent station. It is scheduled to land at Dalian on the 16th and arrive in Harbin on the 20th. (15th Dispatch)

Russian Guerrillas Appear in the Eastern Section of the Chinese Eastern Railway

(Harbin) News from Russian sources here claims that there are two or three guerrilla groups in the eastern section of the Chinese Eastern Railway, each led by a Russian. One is named Solohub, and the other is named Korff. Both are skilled in field warfare. During the Kolchak era, they commanded troops. Solohub was known for his bravery when resisting the White Russians and Allied forces. He once drove a local ice cart with two or three others, traveling through the villages and towns of the Spassk region, capturing Japanese and White Russians, dragging them onto the ocean until the captured died. It is reported that these two Russians are currently active between Suifenhe and Muling, and sometimes expand their activities to Hengdaohezi. It is also reported that there are three Korean partisan groups launching uprisings south of Suifenhe. (15th Reuters Dispatch)

Soviet Union Denies Ma Zhanshan is in Russian Territory

(Moscow) TASS has obtained a formal statement from the Soviet government denying the recent reports from various news agencies and press organizations that General Ma Zhanshan has fled to Blagoveshchensk and has had contact with the Soviet Union. According to the statement, these reports are entirely fabricated. General Ma is neither in Blagoveshchensk nor in any other part of Soviet territory. The rumors about General Ma's relationship with Soviet representatives are not only completely unfounded but also contain provocative elements. The official here now believes that the origin of these rumors is the same as the secret transport of munitions from Dalian by the Japanese to supply General Ma five months ago, which was then attributed to Soviet assistance. These are all Japanese plots. (14th TASS Dispatch)

His authority directly overrides the State Council and the Executive Government. Anyone who wishes to meet with Puyi must first provide their name, resume, and the reason and purpose of their visit in detail. Komai reviews the request, and if it is not approved, it is returned. If approved, a meeting is scheduled. During the meeting, four Japanese individuals stand beside Puyi, providing strict surveillance. If one of them raises a hand, the visitor must leave immediately, regardless of whether the conversation between the host and guest is finished. Important Foreign Telegrams

Soviet Russian Armaments Factory Hurriedly Manufactures Poison Gas Shells

Careless Handling Leads to Explosion of a Shell

Over Seventy Workers Poisoned

National News, Moscow, 15th - In recent weeks, a Soviet Russian ammunition factory near喀常 has been rushing to manufacture poison gas shells, exceeding its work quota. Today, a batch of shells was being transported from the factory to a train when, somehow, one shell suddenly exploded. An odorless, colorless poisonous gas instantly spread throughout the area. Workers transporting the shells were unable to issue a warning and immediately collapsed. The remaining gas blew into the lungs, poisoning and killing over ten more people. Fortunately, one person was able to sound the alarm, and workers throughout the factory put on gas masks, averting further disaster. However, over fifty people have been poisoned, and over twenty have died.

England and America Overcome Current Difficulties and Share the World's Responsibilities

Speeches by New Ambassadors to England and America

Reuters, London, 14th - The newly appointed American Ambassador to England, Mellon, gave a speech at the American Club banquet tonight, stating that the people of the world, especially the American people, are watching how the British government and people respond to their difficulties. They deeply admire the spirit of sharing heavy responsibilities and fulfilling their responsibilities to the world. He believes that England has now emerged from its most difficult situation and is gradually entering a path of recovery. America also has its difficulties, but the large-scale programs submitted to Congress by President Hoover are gradually being passed, and once implemented, they will surely lead to a steady recovery. England and America can jointly undertake the valuable task of helping the world overcome its current difficulties. Lord Derby presided over the event, and those in attendance were all prominent figures. The Prince of Wales and Foreign Secretary Simon were also present. Simon stated that Anglo-American relations are extremely friendly, and England is determined to cultivate this pleasant relationship to promote the welfare of the entire world. The Prince of Wales stated that America's appointment of Mellon as Ambassador to England is a sign of the American people's desire to strengthen mutual trust between the two countries and encourage the British people to bear the current problems. A letter from the King expressed his welcome to the newly appointed American Ambassador.

American Secretary of State Arrives in Europe

Expresses Optimism About the World's Economic Recovery

Reuters, London, 14th - American Secretary of State Stimson and former Secretary of State Kellogg arrived in Plymouth, England, today. Stimson will go to Geneva to temporarily serve as the chief American representative at the Disarmament Conference, while Kellogg will go to The Hague to attend the International Court of Justice.

Havas, Plymouth Port, 14th - Stimson arrived here from New York and spoke about the economic situation, saying that the world's decline has lasted for a long time, but now there is a turning point, and an era of prosperity is about to begin. American commerce is now gradually improving, but he only hopes that it will proceed in an orderly manner and does not believe in its sudden rise. Kellogg, who arrived on the same ship, also expressed optimism about the revitalization of various industries.

Havas, Berlin, 14th - German Chancellor Brüning set off for Geneva tonight.

Germany Reiterates Previous Proposal at the Disarmament Conference

Demands Reduction of Armaments

Not Limitation of Armaments

National News, Geneva, 14th - The chief German representative today sent a resolution to the Chairman of the Disarmament Conference, Henderson, requesting that it be put to a vote in the General Committee of the Disarmament Conference. The content reiterates Germany's demand for the reduction of armaments, not the limitation of armaments. It requests that Article 1 of the draft disarmament convention be revised to make its wording more realistic and clear, so that it is clear that the purpose of the convention is to reduce armaments.

Italy Has No Intention of Withdrawing From the League of Nations

But Hopes the League Will Work Harder

National News Agency, Rome, 14th - Foreign rumors claim that Italy intends to withdraw from the League of Nations. Today, Italian officials firmly denied this, saying that the Italian government has absolutely no such intention at present. This rumor is likely due to a misunderstanding arising from a discussion at the Fascist Party Congress about reconsidering Italy's attitude toward the League of Nations Council in October. Foreign newspapers mistakenly interpreted this as meaning that Italy intended to withdraw from the League. It is not known that the Fascist Party has a resolution advocating that the League of Nations revise the peace treaty. It would be unreasonable to say that Italy would unilaterally demand revision of the peace treaty while preparing to withdraw from the League. In short, Italy believes that the League should be more active, especially because the League of Nations Council has shown very little determination and ability in handling major issues and maintaining its dignity. It hopes that it will have more effective activities in the future.

Confidential Document From Japan to England

Japanese Representative to the League Says He Has Heard Nothing About It

Reuters, Geneva, 14th - British Under-Secretary of State for Foreign Affairs Eden stated in the Lower House yesterday in response to a question from Labor Party Member of Parliament Cocks that there were three documents from Japan that were of a confidential nature and whose contents could not be disclosed. The Japanese representative here stated that he had heard nothing about the Japanese confidential documents mentioned by Under-Secretary Eden and did not know what kind of documents he was referring to.

Reuters, Tokyo, 15th - It was learned today regarding the Japanese confidential documents mentioned by British Under-Secretary of State for Foreign Affairs Eden in the Lower House that Japan had not issued such documents. However, the Japanese Ambassador to England, Matsudaira, had verbally conveyed the Japanese government's position to British Foreign Secretary Simon. The content has not been announced, but there is reason to believe that Matsudaira stated at the time that Japan would rather withdraw from the League of Nations than agree to the application of Article 15 of the League of Nations Charter.

White Russian Conspiracy and the Investigation Team

National News Agency, 英斯科, 14th - Today, the Red Party newspaper Bisiweisi's Yabao claimed that there is a new wave of provocation against Soviet Russia in the Northeast, and that the White Russians are the culprits. These people are racking their brains to undermine the good relations between Japan and Russia in order to provoke a war. Public Riot in New Zealand

Queen Street Turns Into a Dark World

Shop Windows All Smashed

Naval Force Assists Police in Maintaining Order

Over Two Hundred Civilians Injured

Reuters, Auckland, 15th - Auckland, one of New Zealand's most important cities, experienced a violent riot today, necessitating the deployment of a naval force to assist the police in restoring order. During the riot, hundreds of civilians were injured, and twenty-three police officers were also injured. Property damage is estimated at no less than 100,000 pounds. The incident originated with a demonstration by civil service employees protesting an eleven percent pay cut. A large number of unemployed people also joined the demonstration, marching near the city hall. Police attempted to disperse them, and a conflict ensued. Bricks and other objects became weapons. Almost every shop window on the usually bustling Queen Street was smashed. Jewelry stores, clothing stores, and tobacco shops were particularly targeted by the rioters. Young men and women rushed into jewelry stores, scrambling to grab items. The chaos lasted for two hours. At night, the streets were dark because all the streetlights had been smashed. In the emergency, police drove fire engines out to suppress the rioters, but to no avail. The authorities urgently called for sailors from warships in the harbor to come ashore and temporarily organized a special police force. Many people have volunteered.

Reuters, Auckland, 15th - By midnight, when a large force of reinforcements, sailors, and citizens had gathered, the rioters had already scattered. It is now estimated that about forty people have been arrested, and over two hundred have been injured and admitted to hospitals. The city is now calm, but Queen Street looks as if it has been bombarded. No fewer than two hundred and fifty large glass windows have been smashed by the rioters. The Royal Naval Reserve has been deployed for defense, and mounted volunteer patrols are patrolling the streets. Insurance premiums for glass windows have increased by fifty percent. Fire insurance premiums are a thousand times higher than usual, so it is impossible to insure.

Reaction to German Government's Dissolution of Nazi Party Military Forces

Reuters, Berlin, 15th - President Hindenburg's order to dissolve the military organization of the National Socialist Party has aroused the anger of party members in the Munich area. Five hundred armed police officers went to the party's office there to search for documents and pointed guns at people, preventing them from leaving. Party members were very angry. Today, they held an election meeting, and the situation was very bad, but the chairman's strong encouragement to remain calm prevented trouble. Opinion in western Germany believes that the government's hostile actions towards the National Socialist Party may instead make people sympathize with Hitler. Although its semi-military organization has been dissolved on the surface, party members will secretly carry out more forceful actions. 克拉格, the Minister of the Interior and Police Chief of Brunswick, although a member of the National Socialist Party, is now complying with government orders and personally carrying out the dissolution of the party's military organization.

Important News

Account of the League of Nations Investigation Team Arriving in Peiping

Scheduled to Stay in Peiping for Seven or Ten Days

Focusing on Collecting Various Materials

Peiping Correspondence: The League of Nations Investigation Team arrived in Tientsin on the morning of the 9th and took a special train to Peiping in the afternoon, arriving at the station at 6:10 p.m. On the morning of the 10th, they visited Zhang Xueliang. The situation is recorded as follows:

Arrangements for Welcome: Upon receiving the news on the 9th that the investigation team would arrive in Peiping that evening, various circles and groups here immediately hung flags to express their welcome. Various important thoroughfares also had pre-hung slogans. For example, the archways of West Chang'an Avenue, Tiananmen, and the entrance of the Beijing Hotel had white cloth banners two zhang long and two zhang wide, with Chinese characters at the top and English in neat font below. At the entrance of the Beijing Hotel, the banner read (Welcome the Impartial and Just League of Nations Investigation Team). The others read (The Chinese People Would Rather Die for Justice Than Submit to the Humiliation of Power), (The Chinese People Will Never Recognize Treaties Imposing National Humiliation Through Power), (The Chinese People Resist Japan to Uphold Justice), etc. The East Railway Station was newly painted, and a flower archway was erected outside the fence, with the word (Welcome) written above and (Welcome) in English below. The white cloth banner outside the station read (Welcome the League of Nations Investigation Team, Messengers of Peace), also in Chinese and English. The train stopped at the northernmost platform. A pine branch archway was erected at the platform gate, and a completely English white cloth welcome banner was hung outside the platform. After the special train stopped, the small electric lights were all lit, and the red and green colors reflected each other, making it bright and dazzling. Around 5:00 p.m., the area around West Chang'an Avenue gradually saw people from all walks of life wearing top hats and formal suits, or round-topped hats and Qing-style jackets with light red circular badges (entry permits) pinned to their lapels, rushing towards the Qianmen area. Small vendors in the Dongdan and Dong'anmen areas covered their tables with clean white foreign cloth, neatly and uniformly, a rare sight in Peiping. After 5:00 p.m., the station gate was closed to all but authorized personnel. There were about four or five hundred military and police officers, and three military bands. The two bands on the easternmost and westernmost sides were both from the Public Security Bureau, while the middle band of about forty people, in blue uniforms, yellow hats, and badges, was a naval band from Qingdao. When the special train entered the station, the band on the eastern end began to play. The welcoming personnel had their designated positions. The academic community was on the easternmost side, followed by civil groups, the press, representatives of various institutions, and then the receptionists and leaders of various institutions. The westernmost side was occupied by various embassies. Generally speaking, the more westward the position, the better, and the more important. Not many representatives from the academic community arrived, as all universities and schools had been on strike since the day before, a desolate scene. Most students and others maintained a silent attitude towards the arrival of the investigation team and did not express much. As a result, the eastern end appeared increasingly deserted, while the western end became more crowded. There were a total of five female representatives, one a tall young Western woman, one a plump Miss Xiong, and the others were unrecognizable. There were not many Westerners. There was one among the press, and four or five Japanese, also standing in the press.

Situation at the Station: At about 5:30 p.m., a train pulled into the eastern side of the south platform, seemingly to block the view from the south. At 5:55 p.m., a pilot train entered, and at 6:01 p.m., the military band played loudly and the special train arrived. The special train was dark green and newly built. The interior furnishings were exquisite, and the curtains were all purple. This train has been extremely rare since the transfer of Sun Yat-sen's remains. After the special train stopped, Zhang Xueliang, the Pacification Commissioner of Peiping, first boarded the train to express his welcome to the five committee members. He got off the train in less than ten minutes. The crowd removed their hats, and the military and police saluted. The investigation team then got off the train together, removing their hats to return the salute to the crowd. At this time, Zhang Xueliang had already returned to Prince Shuncheng's mansion by car. After the investigation team left the station, they also went to the Beijing Hotel by car. Lytton was accompanied by Gu Weijun, Mccoy by Diao Zuqian, Claude by Chen Renxian, Hiny by Wang Yintai, and 马列斯可特 by Tang Xin畲. Along the way, the military and police along the streets of the Public Security Bureau and East Chang'an Avenue saluted with their guns.

Gu Weijun's Remarks: Gu Weijun spoke to reporters at the Beijing Hotel at 7:01 p.m. that evening, saying that the investigation team had left Pukou seven days ago and traveled north, passing through Chuzhou, Mingguang, Bengbu, Xuzhou, and Taian. Representatives from all walks of life welcomed them along the way, and they were very pleased with the safe journey. The members of the investigation team praised the comfortable equipment of the special train of the Beining Railway and highly praised the development of China's transportation industry. Yesterday, they passed through Jinan and attended a banquet hosted by the provincial government, and visited Daming Lake. This morning, they arrived in Tianjin, first receiving the three most active gentlemen, and then receiving representatives from all walks of life: Zhang Boling, Hu Zhengzhi, Bian Baimei, and Wang Wendian. Lord Lytton was quite satisfied because the materials obtained were more detailed than those obtained in the South. Afterwards, he attended Chairman Wang's luncheon and left Tianjin at 3:00 p.m. to come to Peiping. They will stay in Peiping for seven or ten days. He hoped that all circles would reduce banquets and give them time to collect materials. Lord Lytton and others are tired from the journey and plan to rest for a day or two before meeting with people from all walks of life separately. Whether they will go to the Northeast for investigation and compile a report in Beidaihe is still undecided. A simple report will be prepared for the League of Nations General Assembly on May 1. As for the refusal of the puppet state to allow me to enter the pass, I asked Foreign Minister Luo, who said that he had not seen any notification from the puppet state. If such a notification arrives in Peiping, we will definitely not accept it.

Prescribed Intoxication: During the investigation team's stay in Peiping, they must focus on collecting various materials. They have declined invitations to banquets from all walks of life in Peiping, except for the tea party hosted by the third wife of Consultant Zhang and the banquet hosted by Director Zhang. The time for visiting scenic spots will also be determined at any time. Claude arrived at Prince Shuncheng's Mansion after 10:30 a.m. because he had gone to the French Embassy and joined the conversation. League of Nations Dissatisfied With Japan

Recognizes Japan's Proposal to Withdraw Troops From Shanghai as a Pretext

Nineteen-Nation Committee Will Have Fierce Debate

Refusal to Let Gu and Manchuria Enter May Worsen Feelings Towards Japan

Tokyo Kokumin Shimbun, Geneva Dispatch: The League of Nations is about to continue its meeting, and the important events are the Sino-Japanese dispute, the Danube River relief issue, and the international labor issue. Representatives from various countries are now gathering in Geneva one after another. British representative Foreign Secretary Simon arrived here by plane on the 11th. Among them, the most noteworthy Sino-Japanese incident is expected to cause a fierce debate after the opening of the Nineteen-Nation Committee. On the one hand, regarding the Sino-Japanese ceasefire conference, the League's intention is that the Japanese army's withdrawal period is vague, and it is believed that new conditions for the protection of the lives and property of the residents in Shanghai and legitimate business are needed. It is recognized as an infinite pretext, so the Chinese representative 顔必will propose a clear date for the withdrawal of troops and put spiritual pressure on it. In order to deal with the meeting, our government has telegraphed Ambassador to France Nagaoka Shunei to attend as a representative. Although the Council is currently discussing European financial issues and has not yet discussed the Shanghai incident, the statement refusing Gu Weijun to enter Manchuria and Lord Lytton is feared that the League Committee's feelings towards Japan will become more and more惡化. Investigation Group's Report on the Situation from Beijing to the West (5)

Appendix: League of Nations' Handling of the Sino-Japanese Dispute

B. Proceedings of the Third Meeting of the Administrative Council

(1) The Conference on November 16th and the Situation After the Meeting. That day's public meeting was merely a diplomatic formality. Aside from the chairman's explanation of the reasons, no debate took place. Therefore, all negotiations were conducted through secret meetings, which were held almost daily.

At the time, our country still insisted on our consistent stance: withdraw troops first, then negotiate. Japan, on the other hand, insisted that we recognize its so-called Five Basic Principles. As for the attitude of Britain and France, they were completely observing the situation. Britain and France believed that the United States, as a Pacific nation, had more interests in China than they did, and had a very strong navy and solid economy as a backing. They felt the US should adopt a firm and clear attitude toward Japan. However, the United States believed that since the Sino-Japanese dispute was being handled by the League of Nations, the League should bear full responsibility for resolving it. The United States could only assist from the side. Britain and France wanted the United States to first express an attitude of alliance with the League of Nations, while the United States wanted to see how the League acted before considering a long-term, independent cooperation with the League.

After U.S. representative General Dawes arrived in Paris, he still maintained the dignity of a Vice President and remained reserved. French Foreign Minister Briand, as the chairman of the Administrative Council and host, felt it inappropriate to visit first. Therefore, after several days of Administrative Council meetings, no progress was made, while in northern Manchuria, the Japanese army was already engaged in a fierce battle with General Ma Zhanshan on both sides of the Nen River.

When the news of the fall of Qiqihar arrived, it was said that Japan had dropped a bomb on the seats of the Administrative Council. General Dawes also visited Briand to discuss countermeasures. The atmosphere became tense for a time. The U.S. Secretary of State made a strict inquiry to the Japanese ambassador to the U.S. At the same time, the Administrative Council's Twelve Committee discussed the application of Articles 15 and 16. However, the powerful

The effectiveness of Articles 15 and 16 in sanctioning aggressive actions was lengthy, so they could not be put forward.

Shenyang, Jilin, and Qiqihar are the three major cities of our country's Eastern Provinces. Now that they have been successively occupied, Japan's dream of ruling Manchuria has come true. In order to appease the powers, Japan changed its strategy and declared to the Administrative Council that the Five Basic Principles could be left for direct negotiation between the Chinese and Japanese governments later. There was no need to force China to recognize them in the Administrative Council now. As for sending an investigation team, the Japanese government could now accept it.

(2) The Situation After the Conference on November 21st. At the meeting that day, the Japanese representative formally proposed sending an investigation team and asked for everyone's support. However, he stated that the scope of the investigation was not limited to Manchuria, but also included the anti-Japanese movement in mainland China. Our country's representative, seeing through the cunning of Japan's policy, replied that the most important thing now was to order the Japanese army to cease military action and withdraw to within the South Manchurian Railway zone. If this point were relaxed and other matters were used as conditions for exchange, the Chinese government could not accept it. As for sending an investigation team, it was a proposal made by China several months ago and could naturally be supported. However, the authority of the investigation team would be considered when the Japanese representative formally submitted concrete measures. However, China only insisted on a scheduled troop withdrawal, and Japan had managed to get the United States to oppose this proposal. The reason was that there were bandits everywhere in the Eastern Provinces, and it was not appropriate to demand the immediate withdrawal of Japanese troops to endanger the lives and property of foreigners. Britain and France also echoed this, and our country's proposal for a scheduled troop withdrawal was implicitly rejected by the powers. At this point in the meeting, Briand asked the Japanese representative to put forward concrete measures regarding the organization of the investigation team as a basis for discussion at the next meeting, and earnestly declared to the Japanese representative that there should be absolutely no further military action during the investigation team's work. When Briand spoke, he revealed a feeling of infinite sorrow, and said that in this turbulent time, the brilliant and upright destiny of the League of Nations was in his hands, so he dared not but act with reverence to preserve it for a long time. He said, "If you representatives can cooperate with me to resolve the current difficulties, then my joy cannot be expressed. The more dangerous the international situation, the more bystanders criticize and even satirize us. Therefore, we will work harder, and the faith of the world's peoples in the League of Nations will be firmer. If you do not believe me, please look at the mountains of telegrams from all over the world that the chairman has received in recent days, expressing their faith and hope in us. This proves the greatness of the spiritual power of the League of Nations. How can we allow people to destroy this power and destroy the hope for the future of mankind, and become sinners for the world?" Briand cherished the League of Nations as if protecting an infant, but the complexity of world politics made Briand unable to find a solution to the Sino-Japanese dispute. It is very regrettable. Preparing for swaps, the bearish side posts three to four taels. Hesitant Situation That Neither Advances Nor Retreats

Silver supply has been easing: Copper coins see new increased prices.

In the past two days, the form of foreign copper coins has shown slight recovery; however, observing this afternoon's situation, there is still no sign of making a strong advance. With such a state of affairs, one that neither advances nor retreats, the sluggish mood of the copper coin market will likely not be dispelled any time soon. The morning market was at 7 qian 03 li 7 hao and a half, while the afternoon market was at 23 li 6 hao and 2 hu and a half; the end result being that compared to the afternoon market on the previous day, conditions had improved by 6 hao and 2 hu and a half. The amount of funds transferred by drafts in the morning market was 321,000 and in banknotes 40,000, while in the afternoon market it was 68 taels in drafts and 20,000 in banknotes. Banks bought and sold a combined total of 850,000 in the two markets, with the majority being purchases. Tea merchants also had a volume of several hundred thousand taels. The silver call loan rate for the morning and afternoon markets remained at 1 qian 5 fen, while the markup initially began at 2 qian but by the end of the session was only at 7 or 8 fen, which shows that the silver supply has been trending towards easing. The volume of traded discounted bills across the two markets totaled more than 2.1 million, with transactions between various banks and foreign firms totaling more than 900,000. Silver funds deposited included more than 2.5 million from Chinese merchants, more than 300,000 from customs duties revenue, more than 3.1 million in various funds deposited from foreign merchants, more than 800,000 in exchange deposits, more than 500,000 in goods deposits, more than 400,000 in transactions among small money shops, and more than 4.1 million received in silver coin public deposits by money shops, with more than 29 million received in silver public deposits. As for the supplementary coin market situation, there were no transactions in either of the two markets for Jiangnan small foreign coins, so the market price remained as it was at 6 qian 1 fen. For Guangdong small foreign coins, the morning market was at 6 qian 1 fen 3 li, while the afternoon market was at 2 li 6 hao and 2 hu and a half; 130,000 jiao were traded between the morning and afternoon markets, and the state of affairs was also easing. The only exception was copper coins, where due to the difference between supply and demand, the large board boldly increased the price by 4,000 wen to 417,000 wen, creating new increased prices not seen since trading began, with more than 34,000 strings traded.

Undisclosed Trading in Securities and Bonds Rises by Another Half Yuan

There were still settlement transactions in Chinese merchant securities yesterday, but only for 10,000 yuan for the compilation and 5,000 yuan for repatriation, and nothing more; as for the undisclosed trading prices, due to the stability of the situation and good market confidence, there was quite a lot of activity, so it continued to strengthen compared to the previous day, improving by approximately half a yuan.

Cotton Yarn Sales Show Little Sign of Improvement

The cotton yarn market is very weak, with the downtrend not yet stabilized, generating feelings of being increasingly hopeless. Due to sluggish actual sales, a depressed situation, and difficulty in circulating finances, commerce has stagnated along all routes, leading to a decline in market confidence and making it very difficult for the market to develop. The amount of yarn held by various factories is steadily increasing, making it even more difficult to stabilize market prices, hence, a more weaving downturn. Fine yarn forms are especially soft. In short, with the current situation far from stability, there is little hope for improvement in yarn sales. Investigations show that all gangs combined bought only 310 bales yesterday, with the market falling by approximately 5 qian. Among the customer gangs, 61 bales went to inland areas, 105 bales to Sichuan, 65 bales to Shantou, 20 bales to the Northern gang, 10 bales to Xiamen, 5 bales to Jiangxi, and 60 bales to fellow merchants.

Shen Xin Continuously Purchases Local Cotton in Swap Deals

The cotton market remained stable, as the trend of native cotton turned bullish, Indian cotton reversed and rose, and gold prices remained strong, leading to a sense of market confidence. However, with setbacks in the yarn market and yarn prices gradually decreasing, manufacturers are generally adopting a wait-and-see attitude. Shen Xin factory, however, settled quite a few Indian and American cottons. As headlining was scarce, they purchased native cotton in swap deals, leading to unusually active procurement and continuous daily purchases. The other factories took very little action. The sales board is recorded below:

Grain: The Rice Market in the Huangpu River Turns Active

South Huangpu: Yesterday's sources came from approximately 30 firms. Transactions on this street, owing to fine weather, turned firm; top-grade Northern japonica rice increased by another jiao. The arrival of Zhongguan white japonica rice was also scarce. Customer gangs and those on this street became even more active, and the market price increased by several fen. Foreign long-grain rice and customer long-grain rice arrived in a flood and sales were sluggish, falling back by half a jiao. Fermented rice for two yuan alcohol households remained unchanged. Market conditions were downstream.

North Market: Yesterday's sources were not numerous. Retailers and dealers in towns and villages are still keen on selecting the top grades; rice from Wuxi and Kunshan in the customer gang sector has firmed up by 2 jiao. Foreign long-grain rice is scarce, with less availability. Stacking is available, with the market presenting a stabilized situation; an early, slightly lighter stock sold smoothly, so the trend called for an increase of 5 fen. The Northern gang's fermented rice for one yuan did neither well nor poorly. Shipping goods from the Lower River were opening with 5,000 shi.

The Surge in Foreign Rice Becomes More Intense

Spot Rice Suddenly Increases by Three Jiao: Futures Jump Up by One Qian Two

Intense Demand for Supply to the Interior of the Yangtze River: Total of 20,000 Bags Opened

Yesterday's conditions for foreign rice became increasingly active. Besides military needs, the demand from real-sales gangs increased sharply. The Han River along the Yangtze River route has been short of grain since last year's floods. Recently, local markets have gradually recovered, with a strong demand for rice. In addition to the amount handled by Hunan and Jiangxi, it is still insufficient for sales; so, there has been a great deal of purchasing in the market in recent days. Besides this, various places along the route north of the river and Zhenjiang Nanjing have all come to Shanghai to purchase. The demand from various regions of Jiangzhe inland and rural villages of this street is also intense. As the production area has a poor harvest and the back route cannot keep up, market confidence is high; hoarding and inquiring has occurred, and the market immediately presents a prosperous scene. Yesterday, approximately 20,000 bags were opened, including 5,000 bags of No. 1 Saigon rice at a price of 11.3 to 11.25 yuan; 300 bags of Jia japonica rice at 11.27 yuan; 15,000 bags of small twisted rice at a price of 10.02 to 10.15 yuan; and average to second-rate grade rice at 10 to 9.9 yuan, an increase of 2 to 3 jiao compared to the previous day. Futures for the May returned goods were 500 tons, with prices at 4 taels 8 qian 5 fen to 7 fen, a larger increase of 1 qian 2 fen from the previous market.

Gradual Increase in Northern Demand for Flour Prices Jump Unceasingly

The flour market presented a scene of further sharp increases yesterday, as the reserves along various routes were not abundant. With spring coming to an end and sales becoming active, Northern demand is gradually increasing. In addition, the quoted prices for foreign wheat are becoming better and the exchange rate is low, removing the ability to control the high prices of flour. (It was previously reported that the Russian side was handling flour shipments to Vladivostok, and current thorough investigations confirm that these shipments were disaster relief flour, approximately 500,000 bags, and had already been exported on the previous and current days). The factories, having already settled standard prices, are naturally happy to call out higher prices during this turnaround. (Reportedly, the factory price for the end of April has already been approved by the customer gangs, opening at 2 taels 1 qian 5 fen 2 li and a half). Therefore, the sentiment is particularly good, with prices for April opening 1 fen higher than the previous day, and then gradually increasing and even reaching a net of 2 taels 1 qian 2 fen and a half, an increase of 2 fen and 2 li and a half. For May, due to the excitement of the market, the opening price was high by approximately 2 fen, and then reached 2 taels 1 qian 5 fen 2 li and a half, an increase of 3 fen. As for the shipyard, yesterday they called out 2 taels 1 qian 5 fen deducting commissions, with both domestic and foreign sales as tight, the following steps are still expected to continue to improve.

Shipment of Over 3,000 Bags of Foreign Wheat Reported for Export

There has been little news from the wheat market for a long time. Yesterday, it was heard that the factory was willing to pay 4 taels 1 qian 5 fen for the foreign wheat in storage, while the traders were offering a fixed price of 4 taels 2 qian, so there were no transactions. However, according to reports from the export industry, over 3,000 bags of foreign wheat were loaded for export yesterday, with the location not yet detailed. If this is confirmed, the following steps are also expected to be noble.

Dried Fruits and Vegetables: Orchid Bamboo Branches High-Quality Goods Are Uniquely Scarce

Recent deliveries of orchid bamboo branches have been lacking, with most of the stock available on the market being medium to second-rate quality. High-quality goods are uniquely scarce, so only a small amount has been opened in recent days. Market prices are no higher than 40 taels, largely because the goods are mixed and have broken shells, mold, and moth damage, making it extremely difficult to get a good price. Sales are also sluggish. It is also reported that in the Guangdong production areas, the flower seedlings are still good, so if they are properly processed, the new goods for this season can be expected to have a bountiful harvest.

Shirting, Blue Striped Cloth, and Bleached Cloth Fall Again

The trends for cotton cloth from our factory have been very weak in recent days, with demand from various gangs light. Chess Game

— ·Wang·Xi·Shen·

Neither peace nor war, a hesitant stance. The center of the chess game is even worse. What is the unpredictable bamboo planned in your chest? Empty flowers reflected in your eyes, enough to be open-minded. The round table meeting opens with people as meat on the chopping block. The country has a square city, and I am a fish. Overturned pottery, the three capitals of Pingzi Fu. If there is nowhere for safety, seek Huaxu.

Ten days of light cold, one day of sunshine. The small building is busy killing the sound of flower vendors. The neon clothes are blown around in three thousand formations. The pavilions and towers are obscured by the clouds of twelve cities. The eyes are filled with the filth of spring, proudly ruling the maritime state. The heart is startled by the fragrant sequence passing Qingming. Most seductive is the corner east of the wall. Butterfly messengers and bee matchmakers have boundless affection.

A Daily Newspaper Reporter's Awakened Words and Hatred of Heaven

At the time of the January 28th Incident, Admiral Nomura, the Japanese naval commander stationed in Shanghai, emboldened by the Sino-Japanese War of 1894-1895 and the September 18th Incident in the Northeast, held no respect for China in his mind. Therefore, even after obtaining complete acceptance of the Four Conditions from various parties, he was still not satisfied, but was determined to occupy Shanghai and then be happy, saying that the Japanese army could sweep away the Chinese troops in Shanghai in just four hours. Who would have thought that since the outbreak of the January 28th Incident, reinforcements had been added more than ten times, and the commander had been changed four times, yet the stalemate continued for more than a month. Our troops had no reinforcements, and Liuhe was attacked, and only then did the entire army retreat. Has the Japanese military's continental dream been realized? When the battle of Shanghai broke out, the Japanese army was repeatedly defeated. A certain reporter for a Japanese newspaper once said that today's China is not the China of the Sino-Japanese War, and the 19th Route Army is not comparable to the dragon flag and braid-wearing troops of the past. The Chinese people have already awakened, and are no longer ignorant of patriotism as they were in the past. The fact that the people of Shanghai fully provided the 19th Route Army with material and spiritual assistance is clear evidence of this awakening. This statement is indeed true, and it is not only the people of Shanghai who can passionately love their country. When Li Xiangrong sings in the capital,

Every time she goes on stage, she first makes a brief speech, urging people to love their country, and then sings an excerpt from an anti-Japanese Peking Opera that she wrote herself, to inspire the audience. (It is quite generous and moving, but the lyrics are omitted due to space constraints.) Xiangrong is just a small woman who sells songs, yet she knows how to love her country. It can be seen that our people across the country are no longer soundly asleep as they were during the Sino-Japanese War.

The Monkey Handler's Words

— Bicheng

Military pigeons and military dogs are often seen in newspapers. Recently, there has been much talk about military monkeys. It is said that monkeys are very agile and can be taught to throw grenades. They can climb quickly and easily, and their small size makes them easy to avoid enemy bullets. I heard that a certain army in our country is starting to train military monkeys. If successful in the future, they will surpass pigeons and dogs and establish a unique position. There should be no doubt about that. However, there is a common saying, "green-bellied monkey," used to describe a fool, implying that no matter how many times you teach them, they will never learn. One day, I saw a monkey handler and asked him if monkeys could perform and whether they had any innate intelligence. I also asked if there were any so-called "green-bellied monkeys." The monkey handler smiled and said, "Green-bellied? You don't know, but we in this business have our ways of testing monkeys. First, we lock several monkeys in a room and feed them. Each monkey gets a clay pot. We teach them that after eating, they must put the clay pot on their heads, or they will be whipped. After teaching them carefully, the monkey handler leaves and locks the door, peeking through the crack. After the monkeys finish eating, some put the clay pot on their heads as instructed, while others don't. The monkey handler then makes a noise at the door, as if to open it. Those who haven't put on the pot quickly grab it and put it on their heads. When the door doesn't open, they take the pot off again. After a while, the door rattles again, and they quickly put the pot back on. The monkey handler silently notes each monkey. Those who are clever and intelligent are teachable and can be trained to perform. Those who wear the pot like wooden puppets without moving are unteachable and difficult to train. Isn't that what you call a 'green-bellied monkey'? Therefore, those who are now training military monkeys should be careful not to take them all indiscriminately and allow 'green-bellied monkeys' to be mixed in."

The Shanghai Battle and Military Weapons (10)

— Yi Zang

Soft-Nosed Bullets: Originally called Dum Dum bullets. The name Dum Dum Bullet comes from the factory in Dum Dum, India. It is a type of pointed bullet with a unique poison. Being hit by this bullet will cause the entire body to swell, and there is no cure. Even touching the bullet will cause the skin to ulcerate. In 1899, during the war between Britain and the Boers in South Africa, this poisonous bullet was used to brutally kill enemy soldiers. The Hague Peace Conference Treaty specified that its use was prohibited. However, it was later used secretly in violation of the treaty. In 1912, the International Peace Conference banned it again. When the European War broke out, inhumane countries violated the treaty again and used this bullet extensively. After the war ended, the Washington Conference in 1922 saw Britain, the United States, France, Italy, and other countries re-signed a treaty banning its use. Unexpectedly, in this Shanghai battle, our soldiers suffered severe injuries from this poisonous bullet.

Poisonous Bacteria: War is originally the most brutal act of mankind, and the use of poisonous gas and poisonous bullets is particularly intolerable in terms of humanity. Recently, an even more potent poison has been invented, called poisonous bacteria. It is made from various virulent infectious pathogens, loaded into a projector, and fired into the vast enemy lines. It not only inflicts fatal injuries on the enemy in combat but also causes the complete death of innocent civilians. However, the exact method of using poisonous bacteria has not yet been announced. It is likely that the bacteria will be loaded into bombs or artillery shells and fired, or dropped from airplanes. Therefore, the future of war is truly unimaginable.

Escape (Continued)

— Cheng Mingxiang

Just thinking about those things made him feel like the national crisis was truly upon him. Qian Ping was even more worried than his wife. All the terrors, troubles, and dangers of fleeing were now swirling in his mind, impossible to dismiss. It had completely erased the courage he had displayed when he volunteered to be the commander of the volunteer army in school when the Japanese first invaded Shenyang. The happiest to hear about the escape were Qian Ping's two children. They knew they would have the chance to go play in the countryside tomorrow, so they eagerly awaited the arrival of morning.

"Young master, there's a phone call from Wang on XX Road," the maid said as they were almost finished packing their luggage at ten o'clock in the evening.

After a long while, Qian Ping came back with a smile he hadn't shown in days, saying, "We don't need to escape anymore, no need to escape!"

"Why?" his wife asked.

"Young master, is the world at peace now, so we don't need to escape?" the maid also asked.

"We won another battle, so we don't need to escape. Besides, escaping is very dangerous. The boats going to the countryside today were completely looted by bandits, it's really terrifying!" Thus, Qian Ping told his wife the news he had received on the phone, saying that X city had been recovered by the volunteer army and that there had been significant progress in military affairs. For the time being, there was no need to escape. When his wife heard that they didn't need to escape, she felt relieved, as if the national crisis had passed. The children, on the other hand, puffed up their cheeks, looking unhappy, as if they had lost their playmates.

All the previous busyness now seemed laughable!

At dinner, the family was still comfortably in their exquisite home. His wife suddenly remembered that Qian Ping was also in the volunteer army and asked,

"What happened to the volunteer army at your school? I don't see them anymore."

"If it weren't for the good news, we would have been having dinner in the countryside tomorrow!" Qian Ping replied evasively. At the same time, a faint smile of shame appeared at the corner of his mouth. He was thinking, "After they counterattack, won't I still be showing off on the drill field as the commander?"

Local Supplement

Words

Former Zhabei

— Rui

Yesterday, I received an article from Mr. Zhong Ji, asking who Zhabei belonged to. I have reorganized and extended its meaning to discuss with readers. The other day, while reading this newspaper, I unintentionally discovered an advertisement. The original text is as follows:

(So and so lawyers are appointed as the perennial legal advisors for so and so company in former Zhabei.)

I was quite surprised to see this advertisement. Although Zhabei, which is an inherent territory of our country, is currently temporarily occupied by the enemy, it is undoubtedly still Zhabei of our country. Because our Republic of China has not ceded Zhabei to any country, and no country has denied that Zhabei is not our territory, then that Zhabei, no matter what, is still entirely Zhabei of the territory of our Republic of China. The meaning is clear, what is left to say. Such a simple truth should be clear even to people who have not studied law. But the advertisement says, "So and so company in former Zhabei." I don't understand what the "former" means. Does it mean that the former was Zhabei, but now it is not? Does it mean that the former was Zhabei of our country, but the latter is not Zhabei of our country? Compared to the latter, what is the date before which it is "former Zhabei" and after which it is "latter Zhabei"? At first glance, the text is quite abrupt. Upon closer examination, the meaning is even more vague. If it is said that the company has ceased operations since the battle of Zhabei, then the "former" refers to the company. But since the lawyers are hired as perennial legal advisors for the company, then the company of the "former" day is still the company of today. If its name still exists, then its existence must still be ongoing, it is not as if after the previous company, there would be a new company. If it is said that the former is the company when it was in operation, and the latter is the company when it is no longer in operation, then the word "former" should also be added to the company's name, not Zhabei's. Furthermore, since the company hired the lawyers as perennial legal advisors, then the legal benefits of the company when it was operating should certainly be protected, and the legal benefits of the company when it has stopped operating should also be protected by the lawyers. If the word "former" is added, then the lawyers will guarantee the company of the former day, while the lawyers would not guarantee the company of the latter day.

In short, the text of our country is very ambiguous. At this critical moment, we must pay due attention to this matter, otherwise it will easily cause people to have doubts.

If the principal debtor, etc., perform according to the settlement, it will naturally not be necessary to execute against the applicant. Criminal Judgment: The Police Department sues Dai Xu for opium case (Main Text): Dai Xu is fined one hundred yuan for possessing opium paraphernalia. The opium pipe, opium lamp, opium needle, and opium tongs, one of each, are all confiscated and burned.
